<div id="review_2166814779" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2166814779" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2166814779?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/24142972-use-of-weapons">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=pb-and-j-dipped-in-hot-chocolate">pb-and-j-dipped-in-hot-chocolate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=the-best">the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=mieville50">mieville50</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=about-guilt">about-guilt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=one-of-the-greats">one-of-the-greats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=banks-culture-novel">banks-culture-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=about-life">about-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=anti-heroes">anti-heroes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2166814779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17041178520762825461">This is my fourth review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12007.Use_of_Weapons__Culture___3_' title='Use of Weapons (Culture, #3) by Iain M. Banks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Use of Weapons</a>. I've not looked back on any of my previous reviews so there is every possibility I am going to repeat myself, so I apologize if you have read some part of this before, but this book is a <u>fucking</u> wonder. <br/><br/>Cheradenine Zakalwe.<br/><br/>I do not think there is a more fascinating character in the history of science fiction than Cheradenine Zakalwe, nor is there a more challenging. He is a man we slowly discover we should hate, yet he is a man I can't help loving. Has</span>
  <span id="freeText17041178520762825461" style="display:none">This is my fourth review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12007.Use_of_Weapons__Culture___3_" title="Use of Weapons (Culture, #3) by Iain M. Banks" rel="nofollow noopener">Use of Weapons</a>. I've not looked back on any of my previous reviews so there is every possibility I am going to repeat myself, so I apologize if you have read some part of this before, but this book is a <u>fucking</u> wonder. <br /><br />Cheradenine Zakalwe.<br /><br />I do not think there is a more fascinating character in the history of science fiction than Cheradenine Zakalwe, nor is there a more challenging. He is a man we slowly discover we should hate, yet he is a man I can't help loving. Has there ever been a rounder character than Zakalwe -- and I am talking in all literature now, not just in Sci-Fi -- with all his growth and folly and guilt and penance and ugliness and beauty? For me the answer is no. He is Macbeth and Caesar; he is Holden Caulfield and Jake Barnes; he is Ed Gein and Genghis Khan; he is Hawkeye Pierce and Jack Burton. He is God ... or, at least, a Messiah. He is everything at once, and I can't help loving him, even though I shouldn't, and that may be Iain M. Banks greatest literary achievement -- making us love Zakalwe. In fact, making Cheradenine Zakalwe likeable is a Herculean task, but that was Banks' goal and Banks' success and Banks' greatest achievement.<br /><br /><i>Use of Weapons</i> gets better every time I read or listen to it (and Peter Kenny's reading is some of the best vocal acting I have ever heard), so please read it, friends, and tell me what you think. And if you don't agree that it is brilliant, read it again, then take your argument to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=China%20Mieville" title="China Mieville" rel="nofollow noopener">China Mieville</a> because he agrees with me, and he will do a better job of beating you down than I can.<br /><br />And P.S. -- don't sit in small white chairs. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17041178520762825461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MlHCYMalMAGNGCVuUEmh0cnXsdokMYM4aScYVVwBbmgId6uyffv5aSozkQ+nvKsOH4hWEuq8DV8yWV7kkUKc8g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5807106.Iain_M_Banks">About Iain M. Banks</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5807106.Iain_M_Banks"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1352410520p3/5807106.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5807106.Iain_M_Banks">Iain M. Banks
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2563579042250222064">Iain M. Banks is a pseudonym of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7628.Iain_Banks' title='Iain Banks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Iain Banks</a> which he used to publish his Science Fiction.<br/><br/>Banks's father was an officer in the Admiralty and his mother was once a professional ice skater. Iain Banks was educated at the University of Stirling where he studied English Literature, Philosophy and Psychology. He moved to London and lived in the south of England until 1988 when he returned to Scotland, li</span>
  <span id="freeText2563579042250222064" style="display:none">Iain M. Banks is a pseudonym of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7628.Iain_Banks" title="Iain Banks" rel="nofollow noopener">Iain Banks</a> which he used to publish his Science Fiction.<br /><br />Banks's father was an officer in the Admiralty and his mother was once a professional ice skater. Iain Banks was educated at the University of Stirling where he studied English Literature, Philosophy and Psychology. He moved to London and lived in the south of England until 1988 when he returned to Scotland, living in Edinburgh and then Fife.<br /><br />Banks met his wife Annie in London, before the release of his first book. They married in Hawaii in 1992. However, he announced in early 2007 that, after 25 years together, they had separated. He lived most recently in North Queensferry, a town on the north side of the Firth of Forth near the Forth Bridge and the Forth Road Bridge.<br /><br />As with his friend Ken MacLeod (another Scottish writer of technical and social science fiction) a strong awareness of left-wing history shows in his writings. The argument that an economy of abundance renders anarchy and adhocracy viable (or even inevitable) attracts many as an interesting potential experiment, were it ever to become testable. He was a signatory to the Declaration of Calton Hill, which calls for Scottish independence.<br /><br />In late 2004, Banks was a prominent member of a group of British politicians and media figures who campaigned to have Prime Minister Tony Blair impeached following the 2003 invasion of Iraq. In protest he cut up his passport and posted it to 10 Downing Street. In an interview in Socialist Review he claimed he did this after he "abandoned the idea of crashing my Land Rover through the gates of Fife dockyard, after spotting the guys armed with machine guns." He related his concerns about the invasion of Iraq in his book <i>Raw Spirit</i>, and the principal protagonist (Alban McGill) in the novel <i>The Steep Approach to Garbadale</i> confronts another character with arguments in a similar vein.<br /><br />Interviewed on Mark Lawson's BBC Four series, first broadcast in the UK on 14 November 2006, Banks explained why his novels are published under two different names. His parents wished to name him Iain Menzies Banks but his father made a mistake when registering the birth and he was officially registered as Iain Banks. Despite this he continued to use his unofficial middle name and it was as Iain M. Banks that he submitted <i>The Wasp Factory</i> for publication. However, his editor asked if he would mind dropping the 'M' as it appeared "too fussy". The editor was also concerned about possible confusion with Rosie M. Banks, a minor character in some of P.G. Wodehouse's Jeeves novels who is a romantic novelist. After his first three mainstream novels his publishers agreed to publish his first SF novel, <i>Consider Phlebas</i>. To distinguish between the mainstream and SF novels, Banks suggested the return of the 'M', although at one stage he considered John B. Macallan as his SF pseudonym, the name deriving from his favourite whiskies: Johnnie Walker Black Label and The Macallan single malt.<br /><br />His latest book was a science fiction (SF) novel in the Culture series, called <i>The Hydrogen Sonata</i>, published in 2012.<br /><br />Author Iain M. Banks revealed in April 2013 that he had late-stage cancer. He died the following June.<br /><br />The Scottish writer posted a message on his official website saying his next novel <i>The Quarry</i>, due to be published later this year*, would be his last.<br /><br />*<i>The Quarry</i> was published in June 2013.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2563579042250222064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
